<Text>We have been taking our dog to Companions for approximately 3 years now and in that time they have dealt with several issues that were age related.  Because of their knowledge and compassion, our dog lived longer and better than what we thought was possible given the medical conditions she had.  Dr. Duffy was our dogs normal vet-she is professional yet really loves animals... she made appointments easier on our dog than any other vet that she had in her 15 years of life.

In the last few weeks, it became clear that our dogs quality of life was suffering.  We made the difficult decision to have her put to sleep. The appointment went as smooth as it possibly could have. We saw Dr. Caruso on a few occasions over the years and she is the one that ended up putting our dog to sleep.  It was a relief to have a vet who didn't care how many biscuits our dog ate while she was shaving her arm and administering the medicine...as long as our dog was comfortable and stress free, that was all that mattered.  Our dog, who was very food driven up to her last day, went to sleep with biscuits in her mouth.

We couldn't recommend Companions any more highly. < Review>
My exhaust gas pressure sensor, Part# 4928594 - easily available for  $19 to $25 dollars online,  was $106 here.   The solitary light bulb they installed for my turn signal was .61 cents.     Add them together here and you'll walk away with a bill that's over $700.

Now, with over 1 million single-owner miles on the T660 that I brought here, it should go without saying that I understand diesel repairs can be expensive.  I'm not even a stranger to Inland and have spoken highly of the company in the past, especially at their Phoenix location.  But this location (Carson - first time here) is really something to take away my breath.

How does a mechanic turn less than $30  dollars worth of parts - the most complex of which installs as easily as a spark plug, into a bill that's over $700 dollars high?

What if we even use an Inland number like $106 for parts?  That still leaves us $600 off total.

It wasn't diagnosis.  That happened quickly.   And this repair was easy.  (See pic)

Drivers, you should expect this kind of billing if you go here.  As other truck owners have noted, Carson's bills are "different."  Your potentially positive experience with Inland elsewhere is irrelevant.< /Review>

< review>
Kitchen Mouse is a vegetarian restaurant on 59th avenue and Fig. Atmosphere is welcoming and relaxing. Interior decor resembles your own kitchen house with accented lights and classic dinner tables/chairs. Similarly, it is well organized, neat and lots of natural light. Outdoor seats are available albeit very limited. Prices are a bit on the high end for HP neighborhood. They accept cash and credit/debit card. Staff are friendly and professional. On a busy day, service can be slow and long lines. You need to order first before you take a table. We ordered their three stacks House Pancakes, made of oat, buckwheat, and corn flour with blue berries/strawberries, toasted coconut and maple syrup; and two scrambled eggs. Pancakes were flavorful and fluffy and thick; the eggs are perfectly cooked and their coffee was just good. Overall, if you like veggie breakfast KM is the place to be.<//review>

<Review>The cute, retro kitschy decor is only the beginning at Kitchen Mouse. Catering to the vegan gluten-free crowd, the breakfast tacos can be made with either egg or tofu. I'm neither, so I chose the egg option and added the optional avocado. It was really good. Fresh corn tortillas filled with scrambled egg, lettuce and greens and drizzled with delicious creamy sauce.  I also opted for a strawberry corn muffin that was also delicious. My friend ordered the Sunshine Bowl which had seasonal fruit nestled on top of fresh homemade yogurt  and sprinkled with granola. Garnished with chia seeds and an edible flower, she said it was refreshing. She also had a gluten-free chocolate donut that she said was really good.  They offer bottomless coffee and free wifi as well. Definitely recommend Kitchen Mouse.</Review>< Pics>

< review>
HP is on its way to gentrification and Kitchen Mouse is part of this transformation.  Missing a couple of stars NOT because of the food.

Very long line, long wait, would have been nice to have been greeted and informed as it's not clear that you need to wait in line first to order before sitting down. You can't see the sign letting you know this because the sign is at the bottom of the counter and people are standing in front of it.  I thought people standing in line  were ordering to go.

After you order, it's all self service after that.  You need to get your own water, coffee, condiments.  They serve you your food and no one ever comes back to check on you.  Not sure that is the norm or if they're under staffed.

Very cute hipster space, but not a place for strollers.

Now that I know the rules of play, the food was good enough for me to go back and I'll give it another try.< /review>

<review>This is one of my favorite places in Los Angeles. Located in Highland Park, it's the perfect breakfast place for vegans and vegetarians. <user_id>113079907252672660780<//user_id>< name>
Chris Thueson<//name>
<time>1504042686951</time><Rating>4</Rating>< Review>
Excellent vegetarian and vegan cuisine with a hometown country kitchen hippie vibe. I'm by no means a vegetarian, but this is a great place to stop for lunch or breakfast, especially with my friends who have more selective diets. Kitchen Mouse does have eggs for those of us who aren't vegetarian and the Stumptown drip coffee is self-serve and pretty darn good, or espresso and coldbrew if that's your jam.

They've got rice and veggie bowls, tacos, and standard breakfast fare like eggs, toast, and pancakes, or varieties of salads if you're looking for lunch fare.  I most recently had the weekend special, the jackfruit crab benedict. It's different, much lighter than a normal benedict, I don't think it had any bread, just eggs, seasoned jackfruit, and hollandaise on a bed of citrusy arugula. It was delicious, but could have used a bit more seasoning and I wish it came with toast as it wasn't terribly filling.

The line get pretty long on the weekends and seating can be hard to find, best to get here early if you want to beat the brunch rush. You order at the counter, paper menus can be found near the register. They'll give you a number to place on your table.</Review>

<time>1496948566961</time><rating>2<//rating><Review>ALWAYS NOISY.  Have had a hilarious time or two trying to order at the order-counter-register; wait-person and I could not hear each other over the bad music. You have to ratchet down expectations and assume loud group conversations, crying kids, random high pitched electronic messaging to the kitchen, trying to be drowned out with the bland music. I know, I know, I'm not in a library setting, I realize. (Though, they do have a fair collection of diverse cookbooks for your reading pleasure.) During a recent (usually) short wait for food, I downloaded a Decibel measuring smartphone app.  Just as I thought, 65 to 80 db, which the app says ranges /compares normal conversation at 3 feet to vacuum cleaner and alarm clocks (next level is power mower.)
